Against the split 6 or 4-4 front, if we get a defender in the 7-technique position, our tight end will block him. That allows our guard to pull around and block the frontside linebacker. Our wingback will block the second deep man. We count the outside linebacker as the first deep, so our wingback will block the corner here. Since the guard will block the linebacker, our fullback is free to block the safety.

VS. SPLIT 6 OR 4-4, GOAL LINE

We will run the flanker in motion to block the frontside linebacker. Now the fullback will go to the safety.

VS. 4-3 WITH FLANKER MOTION

Another thing we have done is run the option to a non-tight-end side if we get the right defensive look. Some teams will move the Sam linebacker out wide and play roll-up coverage with the secondary. We see this often.

OPTION TO NON-TIGHT-END SIDE

The offensive tackle will chip the rush end if the guard is uncovered. The tackle will chip the rush then block the middle linebacker. The guard pulls and either log-cuts the rush man or kicks the rush man outside. The fullback has the frontside linebacker. If the guard is covered, the tackle has to pin-block the man on our guard. The guard will still pull and block the end man.

When we get into two tight ends, we will give the play to the quarterback. He has the option to call ''either/ or'' at the line to the side where he wants to run the play. We prefer to run the play to an eagle-look side rather than the 50-front side. Sometimes the rush will be a 7 technique. The tight end will then block the 7 technique, putting our guard on the onside linebacker and allowing the fullback to go to the safety. A common blitz we see by the corner and rush is for the corner to loop underneath while the rush goes to the pitch. We teach our pulling guard to read this and go block the corner. The quarterback will option the rush, and the fullback and quarterback will bounce outside the guard's block on the corner.

EITHER/OR VS. EAGLE

 





Page 254

We prefer to run our trap up the middle into an even front. We will usually "either/or" the play so that we can trap the widest 2 technique. We never send in the play to go one way or the other. We always "either/ or" the play. The center will block back to the tightest 2 technique. If they are even, it doesn't matter. The quarterback has the option to go to either side. The quarterback is schooled to pin the tightest 2 technique. We are always pinning our center back on the tightest 2 technique. If you do not do that, the center will have to block the 3 technique, and that is a hard block. That 3 technique can screw up the play because he can get up the field in that position, so the first thing the quarterback has to do is to decide which way he wants to run the play. He can go one way or the other with it.

Our trapping guard is taught to take a drop step, then climb the hole on his second step. His first step is to lose ground and gain a little distance. The second step is right back up into the hole. We do not want him going flat down the line and aiming for one particular man. He is aiming for an area. Our best traps come when the defense loops the tackle outside and plugs the linebacker. Oftentimes we will end up trapping a plugging linebacker.

The tackle on the side that we are going to trap will block the first linebacker on his inside seam. If no one is there, he finds the first linebacker inside. We tell our tackle to aim flat and anticipate the linebacker stepping up. We tell our fullback to aim at the cheek of the center opposite the hole. The quarterback will reverse around and give the fullback the ball as he turns. The guard on the side that the trap will take place will either (1) quick-draw or (2) head-bob, or arm over the man on him, and go to the first linebacker inside.

VS. 4-4

Against a 4-3 front, when we are trapping a 2 technique, we may use a quick draw by our guard not involved in the trapping. Our tackle on the side that we are trapping will be assigned the middle linebacker. Our other tackle will reach the linebacker on his side; if he is heads up to the inside, he will block that linebacker.

VS. 4-3

When we trap against an odd front, we pull our guard and come up on the linebacker. Our tackle on the trap side will reach-block the man on him. Our backside tackle blocks the linebacker on his side. Our non-trapping guard will help the center with the noseguard. Then he runs a "do-dad" block for the backside linebacker.

DO-DAD

If the noseguard is offset, the center will handle the offset by himself. The non-trapping guard will release directly to the backside linebacker.

VS. OFFSET NOSEGUARD

 





Page 255

If we get caught running a trap against the doubleeagle front, we have to block back with our center and guard and trap with the other guard. We do not like to run the play against this defense, but if we do have to run it, this is how we do it. If they shift into the defense and we get caught, we have to run the play.

VS. DOUBLE-EAGLE FRONT

When we run our trap, it is primarily a fullback play, but we do not always run it as a fullback play. We will run it as a one-back play. Say we are in the spread formation or shotgun formation. We can run it from the I back, the no-backs set, or motion no-backs.

SPREAD OR SHOTGUN FORMATION

MOTION-QUARTERBACK NO-BACKS SET

I BACK IN A ONE-BACK SET

Next, I want to talk about our trap option. We run our trap option differently than most people. We have tried to incorporate our trap option into our outside zone package. Our outside zone package is this. If I am a tackle and I am covered and the guard is uncovered, I want to cross over and escape to the linebacker. The uncovered linemen will pull down and overtake. That is our basic scheme. If you are covered, you are going to stretch, cross over, and go upfield to the linebacker. If you are uncovered, you are going to pull and overtake. We try to incorporate our trap option with some outside zone concepts.

Our play starts out looking like a trap play. We option the end man on the line of scrimmage. This option generally gets the ball in the I back's hands. That is what we want because they are the best runners we have. Our quarterbacks are the next best runners. When we go to the open side, our option will get the ball in the quarterback's hands. However, this is the option to the tight-end side, where we are going to get the ball to the I back most of the time. Our tight end will try to get the outside linebacker on his side. The trap action will hold the linebackers, so the tight end has a good chance of getting the outside linebacker.

If we are running the option play to our right, the left tackle and left guard have to base the men on them. Oftentimes the left guard is uncovered, so he can work with the center. If the center is getting help from our left guard, then the center will rip-reach and escape, and the left guard will pull or overtake. The right guard knows that if the center is not working with him, he has to rip-reach on the man on him. If the defender is a wide 3 technique, the guard will usually cut the man on him. The right tackle will check for the outside linebacker plugging and then go to the middle linebacker. The tight end has the outside linebacker.

Against a 4-4 front, we see the linebacker more on the line. The backside guard and tackle base up. The fullback comes off the fake and tries to find the backside linebacker. The quarterback shows trap action and comes outside.

 





Page 256

TRAP OPTION VS. 4-4

Now, we are going to option the end man on the line. We are going to pull and escape with the guard on the linebacker. We pull and overtake the center. Between the guard and tackle on the play side, we should get the linebacker blocked. If the guard cannot get the linebacker on the play side, he should go to the backside linebacker.

The thing we like about this play is this. The action of the backs holds the linebackers in place. We can get the play walled off. We will option against the linebacker if he is on the line of scrimmage. If he is walked off, the tight end will go block him. That is the way we attack the 4-4 with the linebacker off the line.

The last trap I want to talk about is our tackle trap. The play looks like the inside zone to one side. There is a definite cutback. We look at where the defense lines up on our guard in the area where we are going to trap. If they line up in a 3 technique, the pulling tackle will go up inside on a linebacker. If he lines up heads up to the inside, we will trap on the line of scrimmage. Let me show you three situations so you can see how it works. We have tackles that are mobile and can run this play.

First, I will show you the play against the eagle look. The tackle on the split side is in a 3 technique. This means that we are going to trap the linebacker with our offside tackle. The nose is generally offset. The center takes the offset nose by himself. The play starts out looking like an inside zone play to the tight-end side. The strong-side guard steps outside, checks for the tackle slanting down inside, and then takes on the linebacker. 

TACKLE TRAP VS. EAGLE FRONT

The quarterback brings the ball straight back to the tailback, as deep as he can get it to him, and lets the tailback read the play. The tailback aims at the strongside guard and cuts it back behind the tackle's trap block. The fullback fills off the tackles. The tailback starts off to the strong side and cuts back behind the tackle's block. The split-side guard and tackle take the 3 and 5 techniques. They show a quick-pass setup, then come off and block those two linemen.

TACKLE TRAP VS. 4-4 FRONT

Here we have a noseguard who is offset. The man is on the center. Again, the pulling tackle is going to block the linebacker. Since our tackle is uncovered, the fullback will block the end, and our end will block the linebacker.

TACKLE TRAP VS. OFFSET NOSE

 





Page 257

VS. 4-3 WITH TWO 2 TECHNIQUES

We do run the tackle trap to the tight end some of the time. Primarily, we run it to an open side. We still use the same rules. If the man is not on the line, the guard will trap the linebacker. Here it is against the 50 front to the tight-end side.

TRAP OPTION TO TIGHT END VS. 50 FRONT

What I would like to do here now is to show you the video of the plays I just covered. I appreciate your attendance. I will be around the rest of the evening, and I will be glad to visit with you and talk about our program. Thank you.
